leader</a> (2001\xe2\x80\x932003, 2005, 2007)</li>\n<li>2\xc3\x97 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_annual_runs_batted_in_leaders" title="List of Major League Baseball annual runs batted in leaders">MLB RBI leader</a> (2002, 2007)</li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Alexander Emmanuel Rodriguez</b> (born July 27, 1975), nicknamed "<b>A-Rod</b>", is an <a href="/wiki/Americans" title="Americans">American</a> former <a href="/wiki/Professional_baseball" title="Professional baseball">professional baseball</a> <a href="/wiki/Shortstop" title="Shortstop">shortstop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Third_baseman" title="Third baseman">third baseman</a>.  He played 22 seasons in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) for the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>. Rodriguez began his professional career as one of the sport\'s most highly touted prospects and is considered one of the greatest baseball players of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez amassed a .295 <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a>, 696 <a href="/wiki/Home_runs" class="mw-redirect" title="Home runs">home runs</a>, over 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Runs_batted_in" class="mw-redirect" title="Runs batted in">runs batted in</a> (RBI), over 2,000 runs scored,  and over 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Hit_(baseball)" title="Hit (baseball)">hits</a>. He is a 14-time <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star</a> and won three <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL) <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">Most Valuable Player (MVP) Awards</a>, ten <a href="/wiki/Silver_Slugger_Award" title="Silver Slugger Award">Silver Slugger Awards</a>, and two <a href="/wiki/Rawlings_Gold_Glove_Award" title="Rawlings Gold Glove Award">Gold Glove Awards</a>. Rodr\xc3\xadguez is the career record holder for <a href="/wiki/Grand_slam_(baseball)" title="Grand slam (baseball)">grand slams</a> with 25. He signed two of the most lucrative sports contracts in history, but his  career was highly controversial. He incurred criticism from the media for his use of <a href="/wiki/Performance-enhancing_drugs" class="mw-redirect" title="Performance-enhancing drugs">performance-enhancing drugs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNadmission_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNadmission-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTadmission_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTadmission-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Mariners selected Rodriguez <a href="/wiki/List_of_first_overall_Major_League_Baseball_draft_picks" title="List of first overall Major League Baseball draft picks">first overall</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1993_Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="1993 Major League Baseball draft">1993 MLB draft</a>, and he debuted in the major leagues the following year at the age of 18. In 1996, he became the Mariners\' starting shortstop, won the major league <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_batting_champions" title="List of Major League Baseball batting champions">batting championship</a>, and finished second in voting for the AL MVP Award.  His combination of power, speed, and defense made him a cornerstone of the franchise, but he left the team via free agency after the 2000 season to join the Rangers. The 10-year, $252 million contract he signed was the richest in baseball history.  He played at a high level in his three years with Texas, highlighted by his first AL MVP Award win in 2003, but the team failed to make the playoffs during his tenure. Prior to the 2004 season, Rodriguez was traded to the Yankees, for whom he converted to a third baseman, because <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jeter" title="Derek Jeter">Derek Jeter</a> was already the Yankees full-time shortstop. During Rodriguez\'s career with the Yankees, he was named AL MVP in 2005 and 2007. After opting out of his contract following the 2007 season, Rodriguez signed a new 10-year, $275&#160;million deal with the Yankees, extending his record for the sport\'s most lucrative contract.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> He became the youngest player ever to hit <a href="/wiki/500_home_run_club" title="500 home run club">500 home runs</a>, reaching the milestone in 2007. He was part of the Yankees\' <a href="/wiki/2009_World_Series" title="2009 World Series">2009 World Series</a> championship over the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a>, which was the first year of the new Yankee Stadium and Rodriguez\'s only world title. Toward the end of his career, Rodriguez was hampered by hip and knee injuries, which caused him to exclusively become a designated hitter.<sup id="cite_ref-DH_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DH-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He played his final game in professional baseball on August 12, 2016.\n</p><p>During a 2007 interview with <a href="/wiki/Katie_Couric" title="Katie Couric">Katie Couric</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/60_Minutes" title="60 Minutes">60 Minutes</a></i>, Rodriguez denied using performance-enhancing drugs. In February 2009, Rodriguez admitted to using <a href="/wiki/Steroids" class="mw-redirect" title="Steroids">steroids</a>, saying he used them from 2001 to 2003 when playing for Rangers due to "an enormous amount of pressure" to perform.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNadmission_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNadmission-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTadmission_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTadmission-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> While recovering from a hip injury in 2013, Rodriguez made headlines by feuding with team management over his rehabilitation and for having allegedly obtained performance-enhancing drugs as part of the <a href="/wiki/Biogenesis_baseball_scandal" title="Biogenesis baseball scandal">Biogenesis baseball scandal</a>. In August 2013, MLB suspended him 211 games for his involvement in the scandal, but he was allowed to play while appealing the punishment.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Had the original suspension been upheld, it would have been the longest non-lifetime suspension in Major League Baseball history.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> After an arbitration hearing, the suspension was reduced to 162 games, which kept him off the field for the entire 2014 season.<sup id="cite_ref-162games_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162games-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After retiring as a player, Rodriguez became a media personality, serving as a broadcaster for <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_1" title="Fox Sports 1">Fox Sports 1</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> a cast member of <i><a href="/wiki/Shark_Tank" title="Shark Tank">Shark Tank</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and a member of the <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a> network.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In January 2018, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> announced that Rodriguez would be joining the broadcast team of <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Night_Baseball" title="Sunday Night Baseball">Sunday Night Baseball</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In January 2017, <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a> announced Rodriguez would be the host of the show <i>Back In The Game</i>, where he would help former athletes make a comeback in their personal lives; the first episode debuted on the network in March 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 Rangers</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-8"><a href="#2001\xe2\x80\x932002"><span class="tocnumber">2.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">2001\xe2\x80\x932002</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-9"><a href="#2003"><span class="tocnumber">2.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">2003</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#New_York_Yankees"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">New York Yankees</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11"><a href="#2004"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">2004</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-12"><a href="#2005\xe2\x80\x932006"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">2005\xe2\x80\x932006</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-13"><a href="#2007"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.3</span> <span class="toctext">2007</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-14"><a href="#Opt-out_controversy"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Opt-out controversy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15"><a href="#2008"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.5</span> <span class="toctext">2008</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16"><a href="#Early_2009:_Report_of_positive_test_for_steroids"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.6</span> <span class="toctext">Early 2009: Report of positive test for steroids</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-17"><a href="#2009_regular_season"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.7</span> <span class="toctext">2009 regular season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-18"><a href="#2009_postseason"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.8</span> <span class="toctext">2009 postseason</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#2010\xe2\x80\x932012"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.9</span> <span class="toctext">2010\xe2\x80\x932012</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#2013"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.10</span> <span class="toctext">2013</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21"><a href="#2014"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.11</span> <span class="toctext">2014</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#2015"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.12</span> <span class="toctext">2015</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-23"><a href="#2016"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.13</span> <span class="toctext">2016</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Criticism"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Criticism</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Use_of_performance-enhancing_drugs"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Use of performance-enhancing drugs</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Biogenesis_baseball_scandal"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Biogenesis baseball scandal</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Charity"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Charity</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Marketing"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Marketing</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Awards_and_honors"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Awards and honors</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Achievements"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Achievements</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Records"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Records</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>\n<p>Rodriguez was born in 1975 in the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Heights,_Manhattan" title="Washington Heights, Manhattan">Washington Heights</a> section of Manhattan to Dominican immigrants Victor and Lourdes Rodriguez.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> He was raised alongside his two half-siblings, Joe and Suzy, from his mother\'s first marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> When he was four years old, the family moved to the Dominican Republic, then to <a href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami, Florida">Miami, Florida</a>. Growing up, Rodriguez\'s favorite baseball players were <a href="/wiki/Keith_Hernandez" title="Keith Hernandez">Keith Hernandez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dale_Murphy" title="Dale Murphy">Dale Murphy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken_Jr." title="Cal Ripken Jr.">Cal Ripken Jr.</a>, and his favorite team was the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jockbio_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jockbio-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the end of Alex\'s freshman year at <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus_High_School_(Miami)" class="mw-redirect" title="Christopher Columbus High School (Miami)">Christopher Columbus High School</a> in \nMiami, he transferred to <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Christian_School_(Florida)" title="Westminster Christian School (Florida)">Westminster Christian School</a>, where he was a star shortstop on the baseball team and played quarterback on the football team.<sup id="cite_ref-Jockbio_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jockbio-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>  In 100 games he batted .419 with 90 stolen bases. Westminster went on to win the high school national championship in his junior year. He was first team prep All-American as a senior, <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">hitting</a> .505 with nine <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home runs</a>, 36 <a href="/wiki/Runs_batted_in" class="mw-redirect" title="Runs batted in">runs batted in</a> (RBIs), and 35 <a href="/wiki/Stolen_base" title="Stolen base">stolen bases</a> in 35 attempts in 33 games. He was selected as the <a href="/wiki/USA_Baseball" title="USA Baseball">USA Baseball</a> Junior Player of the Year and as <a href="/wiki/Gatorade" title="Gatorade">Gatorade</a>\'s national baseball student-athlete of the year. In 1993, Rodriguez became the first high school player to ever try out for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_national_baseball_team" title="United States national baseball team">United States national baseball team</a>. He was regarded as the top prospect in the country.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez signed a letter of intent to play baseball for <a href="/wiki/University_of_Miami" title="University of Miami">Miami of Florida</a> and was also recruited by Miami to play quarterback for its football team. Rodriguez turned down Miami\'s baseball scholarship offer and never played college baseball, opting instead to sign with the Seattle Mariners after being selected in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/1993_Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="1993 Major League Baseball draft">1993 amateur draft</a> at the age of seventeen.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_draft_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r_draft-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_career">Playing career</span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> selected Rodriguez with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_first_overall_Major_League_Baseball_draft_picks" title="List of first overall Major League Baseball draft picks">first overall selection</a> of the <a href="/wiki/1993_Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="1993 Major League Baseball draft">1993 Major League Baseball draft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_draft_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r_draft-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The Mariners signed Rodriguez to a three-year contract worth $1.3&#160;million, and a $1&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Signing_bonus" title="Signing bonus">signing bonus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seattle_Mariners">Seattle Mariners</span></h3>\n<h4><span id="1994.E2.80.931995"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1994\xe2\x80\x931995">1994\xe2\x80\x931995</span></h4>\n<p>In 1994, Rodriguez made his professional baseball debut as a <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">minor league</a> player with the <a href="/wiki/Appleton_Foxes" class="mw-redirect" title="Appleton Foxes">Appleton Foxes</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Class_A_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Class A (baseball)">Class A</a> <a href="/wiki/Midwest_League" title="Midwest League">Midwest League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He was promoted to the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Suns" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacksonville Suns">Jacksonville Suns</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Class_AA" class="mw-redirect" title="Class AA">Class AA</a> <a href="/wiki/Southern_League_(baseball)" title="Southern League (baseball)">Southern League</a>. He played in 17 games for Jacksonville, and was promoted to the major leagues.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> On July 8, 1994, Rodriguez was 18 years old when he debuted in the major leagues as a starting shortstop.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He was just the third 18-year-old major league shortstop since 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He was also the first 18-year-old major league player in 10 years, and the youngest position player in Seattle history.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Rodriguez recorded his first major league hit when he singled off of <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Valdez" title="Sergio Valdez">Sergio Valdez</a> on July 9 at <a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_first_hit_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r_first_hit-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez played in 17 games for the Mariners, compiling a .204 batting average, two RBIs, and three stolen bases. The Mariners <a href="/wiki/Option_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Option (baseball)">optioned</a> Rodriguez to the <a href="/wiki/Calgary_Cannons" title="Calgary Cannons">Calgary Cannons</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Class_AAA" class="mw-redirect" title="Class AAA">Class AAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_League" title="Pacific Coast League">Pacific Coast League</a> (PCL) in August.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In 32 games for Calgary, he had 37 hits in 119 at-bats for a .311 batting average. He also compiled six home runs and 21 RBIs.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_minors_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r_minors-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_Cannons_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Alex_Rodriguez_Cannons_1.jpg/175px-Alex_Rodriguez_Cannons_1.jpg" width="175" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Alex_Rodriguez_Cannons_1.jpg/263px-Alex_Rodriguez_Cannons_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Alex_Rodriguez_Cannons_1.jpg/350px-Alex_Rodriguez_Cannons_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="399" data-file-height="581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_Cannons_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rodriguez batting for the <a href="/wiki/Calgary_Cannons" title="Calgary Cannons">Calgary Cannons</a> in 1994</div></div></div>\n<p>Rodriguez split most of the 1995 season between the Mariners and the <a href="/wiki/Tacoma_Rainiers" title="Tacoma Rainiers">Tacoma Rainiers</a> of the PCL.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He connected for his first major league home run off Kansas City\'s <a href="/wiki/Tom_Gordon" title="Tom Gordon">Tom Gordon</a> on June 12. Rodriguez permanently joined the major league roster in August and got his first taste of postseason play, albeit in just two at-bats. Again, he was the youngest player in Major League Baseball.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> During the 1995 season, Rodriguez played in 48 games, batting .232 with 5 home runs, 19 RBI, and 4 stolen bases.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1996.E2.80.931997"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1996\xe2\x80\x931997">1996\xe2\x80\x931997</span></h4>\n<p>The following year, Rodriguez took over as the Mariners\' regular <a href="/wiki/Shortstop" title="Shortstop">shortstop</a> and led the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL) with a .358 <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a>, the highest for an AL right-handed batter since <a href="/wiki/Joe_DiMaggio" title="Joe DiMaggio">Joe DiMaggio</a> hit .381 in 1939 and the 3rd highest ever for a shortstop. He also had 36 home runs with 123 RBIs.<sup id="cite_ref-ap081216_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap081216-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  At 21 years and one month, he was the 3rd youngest AL batting leader ever behind <a href="/wiki/Al_Kaline" title="Al Kaline">Al Kaline</a> (20) in 1955 and <a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a> (20) in 1907, and the 3rd youngest player in history with 35+ homers. He was also the first major league shortstop to win a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_batting_champions" title="List of Major League Baseball batting champions">batting title</a> since 1960, and the first in the AL since 1944. At age 20 years, 11 months, he was the youngest shortstop in <a href="/wiki/MLB_All-Star_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB All-Star Game">All-Star Game</a> history. He also led the AL in runs (141), total bases (379), and <a href="/wiki/Double_(baseball)" title="Double (baseball)">doubles</a> (54) and ranked among the league leaders in base hits (2nd, 215), extra base hits (2nd, 91), multi-hit games (3rd, 65), slugging (4th, .631), RBI (8th, 123), and on-base percentage (8th, .414). Rodriguez posted the highest totals ever for a shortstop in runs, hits, doubles, extra base hits, and slugging, and tied most total bases, and established Seattle club records for average, runs, hits, doubles, and total bases, in a season that statistical analysts consider the best ever by a shortstop.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Sporting_News" title="Sporting News">Sporting News</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> selected Rodriguez as their Major League Player of the Year. He finished second to <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(baseball)" title="Juan Gonz\xc3\xa1lez (baseball)">Juan Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a> in balloting for the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">AL Most Valuable Player (MVP) Award</a>. He finished three points behind Gonz\xc3\xa1lez (290\xe2\x80\x93287), matching the second closest AL MVP voting in history.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_96_MVP_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r_96_MVP-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1997, Rodriguez batted .300 with 23 home runs and 84 RBIs. He <a href="/wiki/Hitting_for_the_cycle" title="Hitting for the cycle">hit for the cycle</a> on June 5,<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_cycle_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r_cycle-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> becoming the second Mariner, and at 21 years, 10 months, the fifth youngest player in history, to accomplish the feat. He was the fan\'s choice to start the <a href="/wiki/MLB_All-Star_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB All-Star Game">All-Star Game</a> at shortstop for the AL team, becoming the first player other than Ripken to start at shortstop in 13 years. It was the first All-Star start of his career and his second All-Star Game in two years.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_97_All-Star_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r_97_All-Star-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1998.E2.80.932000"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998\xe2\x80\x932000">1998\xe2\x80\x932000</span></h4>\n<p>Rodriguez rebounded in 1998, when he set the AL record for homers by a shortstop and became just the third member of the <a href="/wiki/40%E2%80%9340_club" title="40\xe2\x80\x9340 club">40\xe2\x80\x9340 club</a>, (with 42 home runs and 46 stolen bases) and one of just 3 shortstops in history to hit 40 home runs in a season. His 43.9 <a href="/wiki/Power-speed_number" class="mw-redirect" title="Power-speed number">Power-speed number</a> was, through at least 2008, the highest single season Power/Speed Number ever.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> He was selected as Players Choice AL Player of the Year,<sup id="cite_ref-player&#39;s_choice_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-player&#39;s_choice-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> won his second <a href="/wiki/Silver_Slugger_Award" title="Silver Slugger Award">Silver Slugger Award</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_98_Silver_Slugger_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r_98_Silver_Slugger-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and finished ninth in the MVP voting.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_98_MVP_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r_98_MVP-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1999, Rodriguez had a .310 average, 42 home runs, and 111 RBIs,<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> despite missing over 30 games with an injury and playing the second half of the season at <a href="/wiki/Safeco_Field" title="Safeco Field">Safeco Field</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Safeco_open_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Safeco_open-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> a considerably less hitter-friendly ballpark than the <a href="/wiki/Kingdome" title="Kingdome">Kingdome</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sea_park_factors_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sea_park_factors-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> At the time, he was the youngest-ever player to record 100 home runs and 100 stolen bases, at 23 years and 309 days of age.<sup id="cite_ref-alden_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alden-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In April 2015, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Trout" title="Mike Trout">Mike Trout</a> reached the same milestone at 23 years and 253 days old.<sup id="cite_ref-alden_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alden-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez entered 2000 as the cornerstone player of the Mariners franchise,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> which had recently traded superstars <a href="/wiki/Randy_Johnson" title="Randy Johnson">Randy Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ken_Griffey_Jr" class="mw-redirect" title="Ken Griffey Jr">Ken Griffey Jr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez put up great numbers as the team\'s remaining superstar, hitting 41 HR with 132 RBIs and a .316 batting average.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He set a career high for <a href="/wiki/Base_on_balls" title="Base on balls">walks</a> (100) and became the only shortstop to have 100 runs, RBI, and walks in the same season.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> He hit well in the playoffs as well (.409 batting average and .773 slugging percentage),<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> but Seattle lost to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2000_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2000 American League Championship Series">2000 American League Championship Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> He was selected as the Major League Player of the Year by <i><a href="/wiki/Baseball_America" title="Baseball America">Baseball America</a></i> and finished third in the AL MVP voting.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_2000_MVP_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r_2000_MVP-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas_Rangers">Texas Rangers</span></h3>\n<p>Rodriguez became a <a href="/wiki/Free_agent" title="Free agent">free agent</a> after the 2000 season. He eventually signed with the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a>, who had fallen to last place in their division in 2000. The contract was at the time the most lucrative contract in sports history: a 10-year deal worth $252&#160;million. The deal was worth $63&#160;million more than the second-richest baseball deal.<sup id="cite_ref-ARodRangers_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARodRangers-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The contract was highly criticized, because it tied up valuable payroll space that could have been spent to improve other areas, such as pitching.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In an article written eight years later, Rodriguez said he regretted signing with the Texas Rangers and wished he had signed with the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> instead, and that he had heeded the advice of his agent, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Boras" title="Scott Boras">Scott Boras</a>. (See <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez#Opt-out_controversy" title="Alex Rodriguez">Opt out controversy</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="2001.E2.80.932002"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2001\xe2\x80\x932002">2001\xe2\x80\x932002</span></h4>\n<p>Rodriguez\'s power hitting numbers improved with his move to the Texas Rangers. In his first season there, Rodriguez produced one of the top offensive seasons ever for a shortstop, leading the American League with 52 HR, 133 runs scored, and 393 total bases.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He became the first player since 1932 with 50 homers and 200 hits in a season, just the third shortstop to ever lead the league in homers, and was just the second AL player in the last 34 seasons (beginning 1968) to lead the league in runs, homers, and total bases; his total base figure is the most ever for a major league shortstop. His 52 homers made him the sixth youngest to ever reach 50 homers and were the highest total ever by a shortstop, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Banks" title="Ernie Banks">Ernie Banks</a>\' record of 47 in 1958, and also the most ever for an infielder other than a 1st baseman, breaking Phillies 3B <a href="/wiki/Mike_Schmidt" title="Mike Schmidt">Mike Schmidt</a>\'s mark of 48 in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> It was his 5th 30-homer campaign, tying Banks for most ever by a shortstop. He also tied for the league lead in extra-base hits (87) and ranked third in RBIs (135) and slugging (.622). He was also among the AL leaders in hits (4th, 201), average (7th, .318), and on-base percentage (8th, .399). He established Rangers club records for homers, runs, total bases, and <a href="/wiki/Hit_by_pitch" title="Hit by pitch">hit by pitches</a>, had the 2nd most extra-base hits, and the fourth-highest RBI total. He led the club in runs, hits, doubles (34), homers, RBI, slugging, and on-base percentage and was second in walks (75), stolen bases (18), and game-winning RBI (14) while posting career highs for homers, RBI, and total bases. Rodriguez started 161 games at shortstop and one as the <a href="/wiki/Designated_hitter" title="Designated hitter">DH</a>, the only major league player to start all of his team\'s games in 2001.\n</p><p>Rodriguez followed the previous year with a major league-best 57 HR, 142 RBIs and 389 total bases in 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> becoming the first player to lead the majors in all three categories since 1984. His nine home runs in April matched a team record that was shared (through 2008) with <a href="/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Iv\xc3\xa1n Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Iv\xc3\xa1n Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> (2000), <a href="/wiki/Carl_Everett" title="Carl Everett">Carl Everett</a> (2003), and <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kinsler" title="Ian Kinsler">Ian Kinsler</a> (2007). He had the 6th-most home runs in AL history, the most since <a href="/wiki/Roger_Maris" title="Roger Maris">Roger Maris</a>\' league record 61 in 1961 and the most ever for a shortstop for the 2nd straight year. He won the <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth_Home_Run_Award" title="Babe Ruth Home Run Award">Babe Ruth Home Run Award</a> for leading MLB in homers that season.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> He also won his first <a href="/wiki/Gold_Glove_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Glove Award">Gold Glove Award</a>, awarded for outstanding defense.\n</p><p>His 109 home runs in 2001\xe2\x80\x9302 are the most ever by an American League right-handed batter in consecutive seasons. However, the Rangers finished last in the <a href="/wiki/American_League_West" title="American League West">AL Western division</a> in both years, a showing that likely cost Rodriguez the <a href="/wiki/MVP" class="mw-redirect" title="MVP">MVP</a> award in 2002 when he finished second to fellow shortstop <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Tejada" title="Miguel Tejada">Miguel Tejada</a>, whose 103-win <a href="/wiki/Oakland_A%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Oakland A&#39;s">Oakland A\'s</a> won the same division.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2003">2003</span></h4>\n<p>The 2003 season was Rodriguez\' last year with the Rangers. He led the American League in home runs, runs scored, and slugging percentage, and won his second consecutive <a href="/wiki/Gold_Glove" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Glove">Gold Glove Award</a>. He also led the league in fewest at-bats per home run (12.9) and became the youngest player to hit 300 homers. He was tied with <a href="/wiki/Jim_Thome" title="Jim Thome">Jim Thome</a> for the MLB lead in homers, and he won his second Babe Ruth Home Run Award.<sup id="cite_ref-morrissey_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morrissey-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-baberuthcentral_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baberuthcentral-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following five top-10 finishes in the AL MVP voting between 1996 and 2002, Rodriguez won his first MVP trophy. Rodriguez, a two-time runner up in the balloting by the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Writers%27_Association_of_America" title="Baseball Writers&#39; Association of America">Baseball Writers\' Association of America</a>, joined outfielder <a href="/wiki/Andre_Dawson" title="Andre Dawson">Andre Dawson</a> from the 1987 <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> as the only players to play on last-place teams and win the award.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the 2003 season, Texas set out to part ways with Rodriguez and his expensive contract. The Rangers initially agreed to a trade with the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, sending Rodriguez to Boston for <a href="/wiki/Manny_Ramirez" title="Manny Ramirez">Manny Ramirez</a>, 19-year old pitching prospect <a href="/wiki/Jon_Lester" title="Jon Lester">Jon Lester</a>, and cash considerations. However, the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Players_Association" title="Major League Baseball Players Association">Major League Baseball Players Association</a> vetoed the deal because it called for a voluntary reduction in salary by Rodriguez.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Despite the failed deal with the Red Sox, the Rangers named him <a href="/wiki/Captain_(baseball)" title="Captain (baseball)">team captain</a> during that off-season.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_Yankees">New York Yankees</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_2008-05-28.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Alex_Rodriguez_2008-05-28.jpg/170px-Alex_Rodriguez_2008-05-28.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Alex_Rodriguez_2008-05-28.jpg/255px-Alex_Rodriguez_2008-05-28.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Alex_Rodriguez_2008-05-28.jpg/340px-Alex_Rodriguez_2008-05-28.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_2008-05-28.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rodriguez took over at third base after he was traded to the Yankees in 2004.</div></div></div>\n<p>Yankees third baseman <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Boone" title="Aaron Boone">Aaron Boone</a> suffered a knee injury while playing a game of pickup basketball that sidelined him for the entire 2004 season, creating a hole at third base.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On February 15, 2004, the Rangers traded Rodriguez to the New York Yankees for second baseman <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Soriano" title="Alfonso Soriano">Alfonso Soriano</a> and a player to be named later (<a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_%C3%81rias_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Joaqu\xc3\xadn \xc3\x81rias (baseball)">Joaqu\xc3\xadn \xc3\x81rias</a> was sent to the Rangers on March 24). The Rangers also agreed to pay $67&#160;million of the $179&#160;million left on Rodriguez\'s contract. Rodriguez agreed to switch positions from shortstop to third base, paving the way for the trade, because the popular <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jeter" title="Derek Jeter">Derek Jeter</a> was already entrenched at shortstop. Rodriguez also had to switch uniform numbers, from 3 to 13; he had worn 3 his entire career, but that number is retired by the Yankees in honor of <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a>. This was only the second time in MLB history that a reigning MVP was traded, with the first coming in 1914 when <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Collins" title="Eddie Collins">Eddie Collins</a> was traded to the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia Athletics">Philadelphia Athletics</a> for cash considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2004">2004</span></h4>\n<p>During his first season with the Yankees, Rodriguez hit .286 with 36 home runs, 106 RBIs, 112 runs scored and 28 stolen bases.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He became one of only three players in Major League history to compile at least 35 home runs, 100 runs and 100 RBIs in seven consecutive seasons, joining Hall of Famers Babe Ruth and Jimmie Foxx. The 112 runs marked the ninth straight season in which he scored at least 100 runs, the longest such streak in the Major Leagues since <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a> did it in 13 straight seasons from 1955 to 1967, and the longest in the American League since <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Mantle" title="Mickey Mantle">Mickey Mantle</a> did it also in nine straight seasons from 1953 to 1961. During the 2004 season, he also became the youngest player ever to reach the 350 HR mark and the third youngest to reach the 1,000 RBI plateau. He was elected to the 2004 American League All-Star Team, the eighth All-Star selection of his career and the first as a <a href="/wiki/Third_baseman" title="Third baseman">third baseman</a>. On July 24, 2004, Rodriguez was hit by a pitch from <a href="/wiki/Bronson_Arroyo" title="Bronson Arroyo">Bronson Arroyo</a>, which led to a scuffle with <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> catcher <a href="/wiki/Jason_Varitek" title="Jason Varitek">Jason Varitek</a>, and a bench-clearing brawl between both teams. On defense, he had the lowest range factor among non-<a href="/wiki/Platoon_system" title="Platoon system">platoon</a> AL third basemen (2.39) in his first year at the position.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> He finished 14th in balloting for the AL MVP Award.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In the 2004 <a href="/wiki/American_League_Division_Series" title="American League Division Series">ALDS</a>, Rodriguez was a dominant hitter against the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a>, batting .421 and slugging .737 while delivering two key extra-inning hits. Following the series win, Rodriguez\'s first season with the Yankees culminated in a dramatic playoff series against the team he had almost ended up playing for: the Yankees\' bitter <a href="/wiki/Yankees%E2%80%93Red_Sox_rivalry" title="Yankees\xe2\x80\x93Red Sox rivalry">rival</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>. In that series (ALCS) he equaled the single-game post-season record with five runs scored in Game 3 at Boston.\n</p><p>One of the most controversial plays of Rodriguez\'s career occurred late in Game 6 of the <a href="/wiki/2004_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2004 American League Championship Series">2004 American League Championship Series</a>. With one out and <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jeter" title="Derek Jeter">Derek Jeter</a> on first base in the bottom of the eighth inning, Rodriguez hit a slow roller between the pitcher\'s mound and the first base line. Red Sox <a href="/wiki/Pitcher" title="Pitcher">pitcher</a> <a href="/wiki/Bronson_Arroyo" title="Bronson Arroyo">Bronson Arroyo</a> fielded the ball and ran towards Rodriguez to apply a tag. As Arroyo reached towards him, Rodriguez swatted at his glove, knocking the ball loose. As the ball rolled away, Jeter scored all the way from first as Rodriguez took second on the play, which was initially ruled an error on Arroyo. However, the umpires quickly huddled, then ruled that Rodriguez was out for interference. Jeter was sent back to first base, and his run was nullified.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The Yankees would then lose the ALCS to the eventual <a href="/wiki/2004_World_Series" title="2004 World Series">World Series</a> champion Red Sox after leading the series 3 games to none.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="2005.E2.80.932006"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2005\xe2\x80\x932006">2005\xe2\x80\x932006</span></h4>\n<p>In 2005, Rodriguez hit .321, leading the American League with 124 runs and 48 HR while driving in 130 runs.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He became the first Yankee to win the American League home run title since <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> (41) in 1980. He also became one of only two players in Major League history to compile at least 35 home runs, 100 runs and 100 RBIs in eight consecutive seasons (Jimmie Foxx accomplished the feat in nine straight seasons from 1932 to 1940). Rodriguez established the franchise record for most home runs in a single season by a right-handed batter (broke <a href="/wiki/Joe_DiMaggio" title="Joe DiMaggio">Joe DiMaggio</a>\'s mark of 46 in 1937). His 47 HR from the third base position are a single-season American League record. Rodriguez hit 26 home runs at <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium_(1923)" title="Yankee Stadium (1923)">Yankee Stadium</a> in 2005, establishing the single-season club record for right-handed batters (previously held by DiMaggio in 1937 and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Sheffield" title="Gary Sheffield">Gary Sheffield</a> in 2004). On June 8, at 29 years, 316 days old, he became the youngest player in MLB history to reach the 400 HR mark. 2005 also marked the tenth straight season that Rodriguez scored at least 100 runs. On defense, however, he had the lowest range factor in the league at third for the second straight season (2.62).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On April 26, Rodriguez hit three home runs off <a href="/wiki/2005_Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2005 Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim season">Angels</a>\' pitcher <a href="/wiki/Bartolo_Col%C3%B3n" title="Bartolo Col\xc3\xb3n">Bartolo Col\xc3\xb3n</a> and drove in 10 runs. The 10 RBIs were the most by a Yankee since <a href="/wiki/Tony_Lazzeri" title="Tony Lazzeri">Tony Lazzeri</a> established the franchise and American League record with 11 on May 24, 1936. Rodriguez became the 11th major leaguer to accomplish the feat.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>  Rodriguez won his second <a href="/wiki/American_League_MVP" class="mw-redirect" title="American League MVP">AL MVP</a> Award in three seasons.\n</p><p>The "League Award" was the precursor to the MVP. Rodriguez became the fifth player to win this award with two different teams, joining <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Cochrane" title="Mickey Cochrane">Mickey Cochrane</a>, Jimmie Foxx, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Robinson" title="Frank Robinson">Frank Robinson</a> and Barry Bonds. Rodriguez was also named the shortstop on the Major League Baseball <a href="/wiki/Latino_Legends_Team" title="Latino Legends Team">Latino Legends Team</a> in 2005.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_Talking.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Alex_Rodriguez_Talking.jpg/170px-Alex_Rodriguez_Talking.jpg" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Alex_Rodriguez_Talking.jpg/255px-Alex_Rodriguez_Talking.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bf/Alex_Rodriguez_Talking.jpg 2x" data-file-width="334" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_Talking.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rodriguez reacting to a called strike in a game against Tampa Bay</div></div></div>\n<p>Prior to the season, Rodriguez opted to play for Team USA in the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2006 World Baseball Classic">World Baseball Classic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-davidoff081116_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-davidoff081116-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez was again an <a href="/wiki/2006_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2006 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star</a> in 2006. His 2,000th hit, on July 21, 2006 \xe2\x88\x92 six days prior to his 31st birthday \xe2\x88\x92 was also his 450th home run. Rodriguez became the youngest player in baseball history to reach 450 home runs (surpassing <a href="/wiki/Ken_Griffey,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Ken Griffey, Jr.">Ken Griffey, Jr.</a>, by 267 days), and the eighth player to reach 2,000 hits before turning 31. <a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a> reached the mark while still 29, while <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mel_Ott" title="Mel Ott">Mel Ott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Medwick" title="Joe Medwick">Joe Medwick</a>, Jimmie Foxx, and <a href="/wiki/Robin_Yount" title="Robin Yount">Robin Yount</a> all achieved their 2,000th hit at age 30. All seven are members of baseball\'s <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Hall of Fame</a>.\n</p><p>For the season, Rodriguez finished fourth in the league in RBI (121), fifth in runs scored (113), eighth in home runs (35) and walks (90), and ninth in OBP (.392). He also led all AL third basemen in errors, with 24, and had the lowest fielding percentage (.937) and \xe2\x80\x93 for the third straight season \xe2\x80\x93 range factor (2.50) among them.<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez also became the second player in Major League history to record at least 35 home runs, 100 runs, and 100 RBIs in nine consecutive seasons, joining Foxx. It was Rodriguez\'s 11th consecutive season with more than 100 runs scored, the longest such streak in American League history since <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a> did so in 13 straight seasons (1926\xe2\x80\x9338). Despite this success, it was perceived as one of his lesser-accomplished seasons and was harshly criticized throughout the 2006 season. He has commented that 2006 was his most difficult season as a professional.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span></h4>\n<p>When Rodriguez reported to camp in 2007, he had reduced his <a href="/wiki/Body_fat" class="mw-redirect" title="Body fat">body fat</a> from 16% the year before to 9%. He made light of this fact during a <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">Late Show with David Letterman</a></i> sketch that was filmed during Spring training, which featured him shirtless being rubbed down with suntan lotion. He revealed to the press that he and Jeter were no longer close friends.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez also reduced his high leg kick at the plate, increasing his bat speed, making him less-apt to strike out and a more dangerous hitter.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the Yankees\' fourth game of the season, Rodriguez hit two home runs against the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a> at <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium_(1923)" title="Yankee Stadium (1923)">Yankee Stadium</a>, including his 14th-career <a href="/wiki/Grand_slam_(baseball)" title="Grand slam (baseball)">grand slam</a> to end the game. The <a href="/wiki/Walk-off_home_run" title="Walk-off home run">walk-off</a> grand slam was the third of his career, tying the major league mark for game-ending grand slams shared by <a href="/wiki/Vern_Stephens" title="Vern Stephens">Vern Stephens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cy_Williams" title="Cy Williams">Cy Williams</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez also began the season by becoming the ninth major leaguer\xe2\x80\x94and first Yankee\xe2\x80\x94to hit six home runs in the first seven games of the season. Rodriguez also became the first Yankee to hit seven home runs in the first ten games of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On April 23, Rodriguez became the first player in major league history to hit 14 home runs in a span of 18 games, and also tied the MLB record for most home runs in April. His total of 34 RBIs in April was one short of <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(baseball)" title="Juan Gonz\xc3\xa1lez (baseball)">Juan Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a>\' AL and MLB record.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In a game against the Toronto Blue Jays on May 30, Rodriguez sparked controversy when he shouted during a routine play and an infielder let a pop fly drop, costing the Blue Jays three runs. The Yankees went on to win the game, 10\xe2\x80\x935.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>  On July 12, Rodriguez hit his 150th career home run in a Yankees uniform. This made him the first, and so far only, player in major league history to ever hit 150 home runs for three different teams.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> He became the third player to hit at least 100 home runs for three teams, following <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Evans" title="Darrell Evans">Darrell Evans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez hit his 500th career home run against pitcher <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Davies_(baseball)" title="Kyle Davies (baseball)">Kyle Davies</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a> on August 4. Rodriguez became the youngest player ever to reach 500 homers (32 years, 8 days).<sup id="cite_ref-youngest500_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youngest500-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> On September 25, Rodriguez became the fifth Major League player to record a 50-home run, 150-RBI season when he hit a grand slam.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A-Rod3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/A-Rod3.jpg/220px-A-Rod3.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/A-Rod3.jpg/330px-A-Rod3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/A-Rod3.jpg/440px-A-Rod3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1576" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A-Rod3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rodriguez batting in 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2007, Rodriguez became the first player in major league history to have at least 35 home runs, 100 runs, and 100 RBIs in 10 consecutive seasons, surpassing Jimmie Foxx (9 consecutive seasons). He led the AL in home runs (54), RBIs (156), slugging percentage (.645), <a href="/wiki/On-base_plus_slugging" title="On-base plus slugging">OPS</a> (1.067), total bases (376), and times on base (299), and was 2nd in hit by pitch (21), extra base hits (85), and at bats per home run (10.8), 4th in on-base percentage (.422) and sacrifice flies (9), 7th in walks (95) and plate appearances (708), 8th in intentional walks (11), and 9th in games (158).<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He led MLB in home runs and won his third Babe Ruth Home Run Award.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the season, Rodriguez was named the AL MVP for the third time in his career, receiving 26 first-place votes out of a possible 28.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> He also won the Silver Slugger Award for his position,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> the Players Choice Award for Outstanding AL Player, and the Players Choice Award for Player of the Year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Opt-out_controversy">Opt-out controversy</span></h4>\n<p>The 2007 season marked the last year of Rodriguez\'s 10-year, $252&#160;million contract before he opted out and became a  free agent again. Rodriguez had repeatedly stated during the <a href="/wiki/2007_MLB_Season" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 MLB Season">2007 season</a> that he would like to remain a Yankee for the rest of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>  On October 28, 2007, Rodriguez\'s agent, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Boras" title="Scott Boras">Scott Boras</a>, announced that he would not renew his contract with the Yankees citing that he "was unsure of the future composition" of the team. He received a slew of criticism from fans and writers alike not only for opting out, but also for not meeting with Yankee management before he did. He was further criticized for the timing of his announcement, during the eighth inning of Game Four of the <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Series" title="2007 World Series">World Series</a>, as the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> were wrapping up their victory over the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a>; even MLB\'s chief operating officer, Bob DuPuy, called it an attempt by Boras to "try to put his selfish interests and that of one individual player above the overall good of the game."<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Teammate <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rivera" title="Mariano Rivera">Mariano Rivera</a> convinced Rodriguez to contact the New York Yankees ownership.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> He contacted them directly, bypassing Boras (Boras also apologized for the timing of the announcement). Subsequently, Rodriguez issued a statement on his website, saying that he wished to stay with the Yankees.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On November 15, 2007, the New York Yankees and Rodriguez agreed on the "basic framework" of a 10-year, $275&#160;million contract that would have him playing until he is 42.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The contract, finalized December 13, includes various multimillion-dollar incentives for breaking career home run milestones.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2008">2008</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_batting_stance_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Alex_Rodriguez_batting_stance_2008.jpg/170px-Alex_Rodriguez_batting_stance_2008.jpg" width="170" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Alex_Rodriguez_batting_stance_2008.jpg/255px-Alex_Rodriguez_batting_stance_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Alex_Rodriguez_batting_stance_2008.jpg/340px-Alex_Rodriguez_batting_stance_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1437" data-file-height="2560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_batting_stance_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rodriguez at bat in 2008</div></div></div>\n<p>Rodriguez hit his 549th home run in a September 3, 2008 game against the <a href="/wiki/2008_Tampa_Bay_Rays_season" title="2008 Tampa Bay Rays season">Tampa Bay Rays</a>. The opposing manager objected that the ball was foul, and for the first time in MLB history, <a href="/wiki/Instant_replay#Baseball" title="Instant replay">instant replay</a> (a process officially introduced a few days earlier) was used to review the play and uphold the umpires\' ruling.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>  He was one of only four batters in the AL to have at least 18 home runs and 18 stolen bases in both 2007 and 2008, along with <a href="/wiki/Torii_Hunter" title="Torii Hunter">Torii Hunter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kinsler" title="Ian Kinsler">Ian Kinsler</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grady_Sizemore" title="Grady Sizemore">Grady Sizemore</a>. Rodriguez hit a home run every 14.6 at-bats in 2008, the second best ratio on the team behind <a href="/wiki/Jason_Giambi" title="Jason Giambi">Jason Giambi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100random_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100random-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez played 138 games during the 2008 season with a .302 average, 35 home runs, 103 RBI, and an AL best .573 slugging percentage.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_2009:_Report_of_positive_test_for_steroids">Early 2009: Report of positive test for steroids</span></h4>\n<p>On February 7, 2009, <i>Sports Illustrated</i> reported that Rodriguez tested positive for <a href="/wiki/Testosterone_(medication)" title="Testosterone (medication)">testosterone</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Anabolic_steroids" class="mw-redirect" title="Anabolic steroids">anabolic steroid</a> <a href="/wiki/Primobolan" class="mw-redirect" title="Primobolan">Primobolan</a> in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-SIsteroids_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SIsteroids-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez\'s name appears on a government-sealed list of 104 major-league players (out of 1200 tested<sup id="cite_ref-Glanville_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glanville-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>) who came up positive for performance-enhancing drugs. The report was compiled as part of Major League Baseball\'s 2003 survey to see whether mandatory random drug testing program might be necessary. At the time, there was no penalty or punishment for a positive steroid test. Rodriguez did not immediately confirm the allegations, deferring at first to the players\' union.<sup id="cite_ref-SIsteroids_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SIsteroids-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTsteroids_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTsteroids-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Two days after the allegations, Rodriguez admitted to steroid use from 2001 until 2003, claiming that he ceased using such substances after spring training that year.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNadmission_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNadmission-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTadmission_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTadmission-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2009_regular_season">2009 regular season</span></h4>\n<p>Prior to the 2009 season, Rodriguez was scheduled to represent the Dominican Republic in the <a href="/wiki/2009_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2009 World Baseball Classic">2009 World Baseball Classic</a>, but he was forced to withdraw when an MRI revealed a <a href="/wiki/Cyst" title="Cyst">cyst</a> in his right hip. When he went to have the cyst drained, it was discovered that he was also suffering from a <a href="/wiki/Acetabular_labrum" title="Acetabular labrum">torn labrum</a> in the same hip. Rodriguez opted to undergo an arthroscopic procedure with a recovery period of six to nine weeks, instead of the usual three to four months.<sup id="cite_ref-surgery_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-surgery-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>  Although the procedure should have allowed him to make it through the season without any complications, he required a second, more extensive surgery in the off-season.<sup id="cite_ref-surgery_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-surgery-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After missing <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">spring training</a> and the first month of the season, Rodriguez returned to the Yankees in a May 8 game against the <a href="/wiki/2009_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2009 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore Orioles</a> and hit a three-run home run on the first pitch of his first at-bat. The Yankees had stumbled to a 13\xe2\x80\x9315 record in Rodriguez\' absence, and his return fortified the lineup and provided much-needed protection for three-hole hitter <a href="/wiki/Mark_Teixeira" title="Mark Teixeira">Mark Teixeira</a>, who was a notoriously slow starter. Rodriguez also supplied some late-game heroics. On May 16, his two-run <a href="/wiki/Walk-off_home_run" title="Walk-off home run">walk-off home run</a> in the bottom of the eleventh inning gave the Yankees a 6\xe2\x80\x934 win over the <a href="/wiki/2009_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="2009 Minnesota Twins season">Minnesota Twins</a>. One week later, he hit a game-tying solo home run in the bottom of the ninth off <a href="/wiki/2009_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2009 Philadelphia Phillies season">Philadelphia Phillies</a> closer <a href="/wiki/Brad_Lidge" title="Brad Lidge">Brad Lidge</a> in a game the Yankees would go on to win, 5\xe2\x80\x934.\n</p><p>By early June, the Yankees had surged to first place in the <a href="/wiki/AL_East" class="mw-redirect" title="AL East">AL East</a>. The club\'s fortunes changed later in the month, when Rodriguez fell into a slump that saw his batting average plummet as the Yankees fell to second place. On June 23, Rodriguez became the eighth active player to reach 8,000 career at-bats in the seventh inning of the Yankees and Braves game.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>  On June 25, Rodriguez belted homer 563 of his career, off <a href="/wiki/2009_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2009 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a> starter <a href="/wiki/Derek_Lowe" title="Derek Lowe">Derek Lowe</a>, and tying <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> for 11th on the all-time home run list.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> On June 26, Rodriguez surpassed Jackson for 11th on the all-time home run list, against the <a href="/wiki/2009_New_York_Mets_season" title="2009 New York Mets season">New York Mets</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Subway_Series" title="Subway Series">Subway Series</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> and against the Angels on July 11, Rodriguez passed <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Palmeiro" title="Rafael Palmeiro">Rafael Palmeiro</a> for 10th place;<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> it was his 65th home run against Anaheim, the most by any active player against an opponent.\n</p><p>On October 4, 2009, during the final game of the season, Rodriguez hit two home runs in the sixth inning that drove in seven runs, setting an American League record for most RBI by a batter in a single inning, and giving him his 12th consecutive season, 13 overall, of reaching 30 home runs and 100 RBIs, breaking a tie with <a href="/wiki/Manny_Ramirez" title="Manny Ramirez">Manny Ramirez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Foxx" title="Jimmie Foxx">Jimmie Foxx</a> for the most in MLB history.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2009_postseason">2009 postseason</span></h4>\n<p>Dating back to Game 4 of the 2004 AL Championship Series, Rodriguez had batted with 38 runners on base over a span of 61 postseason at-bats. He stranded every one of them, going 0-for-29 with runners on base.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>  However, in the first game of the <a href="/wiki/2009_American_League_Division_Series" title="2009 American League Division Series">2009 ALDS</a> against Minnesota, he hit two RBI singles \xe2\x88\x92 both coming with two outs. In Game 2, he hit an RBI single in the sixth, and hit a game-tying homer off closer <a href="/wiki/Joe_Nathan" title="Joe Nathan">Joe Nathan</a> in the bottom of the ninth inning. In Game 3, he again hit a game-tying home run. In the <a href="/wiki/2009_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2009 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>, Rodriguez hit his third game-tying HR of the postseason in Game 2 in the bottom of the 11th against <a href="/wiki/2009_Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim season">Angels</a> closer <a href="/wiki/Brian_Fuentes" title="Brian Fuentes">Brian Fuentes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> For the series, he batted 9\xe2\x80\x9321 (.429) with three home runs and six runs batted in.\n</p><p>The Yankees faced the Phillies in the <a href="/wiki/2009_World_Series" title="2009 World Series">World Series</a>. In Game 3, Rodriguez hit what appeared to be a double off a camera perched atop the outfield wall, but after protest by Yankee manager <a href="/wiki/Joe_Girardi" title="Joe Girardi">Joe Girardi</a>, the play was reviewed and ruled a home run. In Game 4, Rodriguez drove in the go-ahead run with two outs in the 9th inning off closer <a href="/wiki/Brad_Lidge" title="Brad Lidge">Brad Lidge</a>. The Yankees would go on to win the game 7\xe2\x80\x934 to take a 3-games-to-1 lead in the series. Despite a 2\xe2\x80\x934 performance with three RBI in Game 5, the Yankees lost 8\xe2\x80\x936 to force the Series to return to the Bronx for Game 6. Rodriguez was 1\xe2\x80\x932 with 2 walks and two runs scored in Game 6, as the Yankees went on to defeat the Phillies 7\xe2\x80\x933 for their 27th World Series Championship, the first of Rodriguez\'s career. Having reversed his postseason misfortunes, he was the <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth_Award" title="Babe Ruth Award">Babe Ruth Award</a> winner as the 2009 postseason MVP,<sup id="cite_ref-ap012410_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap012410-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> in which he batted .365 with six home runs and 18 RBI.<sup id="cite_ref-kruth080716_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kruth080716-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="2010.E2.80.932012"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010\xe2\x80\x932012">2010\xe2\x80\x932012</span></h4>\n<p>On August 4, 2010, on the 3-year anniversary of his 500th home run, Rodriguez became the seventh player in major league history to hit 600 home runs, hitting number 600 off <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Marcum" title="Shaun Marcum">Shaun Marcum</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a>, becoming the youngest player to do so at 35 years and 8 days old. On August 14, Rodriguez hit three home runs in a game against the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>. In the top of the 6th, he hit his first, a solo dinger to left center. In the top of the 7th, he hit his second, a two-run shot to dead center. In the top of the 9th, he hit his third, a towering two-run blast into the waterfall in <a href="/wiki/Kauffman_Stadium" title="Kauffman Stadium">Kauffman Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>  On September 6, he recorded his 100th RBI; it was the 14th year he had reached the mark, the most times of any player in baseball history. On Sep 29, he hit his 30th home run of the season, recording his major league record 13th straight year of at least 30 home runs and 100 RBIs, breaking a tie with <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Foxx" title="Jimmie Foxx">Jimmie Foxx</a>, who had 12 seasons.\n</p><p>In 2011, Rodriguez batted .295 with 13 home runs and 52 RBIs prior to the All-Star break. Despite good production, Rodriguez suffered his longest single season home run drought of his career by not hitting one in 85 at-bats. Although elected to start the game, Rodriguez opted for arthroscopic surgery on his knee to repair a torn meniscus that impacted his power, and was placed on the disabled list.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> On top of recovery, Rodriguez was facing serious allegations that he participated in illegal, underground poker games. One of those games reportedly turned violent and cocaine was openly used. However, Rodriguez denied through a representative that he ever participated in illegal poker games. An MLB Executive has said that if Rodriguez was indeed proven guilty, he may face a suspension; MLB had warned Rodriguez in 2005 not to participate in such games.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez returned to the Yankees on August 21, playing third base against the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a>, going 0-for-4. He sustained another injury with a jammed thumb while trying to make a play in that game. He returned to the Yankees on August 25, going 2-for-4 with 2 singles in a win for the Yankees over the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a>. On August 26, Rodriguez hit his first home run since coming off the disabled list, a solo shot off <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Hunter_(baseball)" title="Tommy Hunter (baseball)">Tommy Hunter</a>. He concluded the season with 16&#160;home runs and 62&#160;RBIs in 99&#160;games, ending his major league-record streak of 13&#160;straight seasons of 30&#160;homers and 100&#160;RBIs.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez hit his 23rd career grand slam off <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a> relief pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Venters" title="Jonny Venters">Jonny Venters</a> on June 12, 2012, which tied <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a> for the most in MLB history.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In a road loss versus the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> on July 24, 2012, Rodriguez took a hit to the hand during an eighth inning at bat versus Seattle starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a>. The injury was later described as a non-displaced fracture.<sup id="cite_ref-Hand_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hand-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez was placed on the disabled list. Earlier in the same game, Hernandez struck out Rodriguez in the sixth inning, making Rodriguez the fifth player to record 2,000 career strikeouts in MLB history.<sup id="cite_ref-Hand_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hand-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 2012 postseason, Rodriguez was removed for a pinch hitter multiple times and did not start many times.
