He batted 3-for-25 overall, and went 0-for-18 with 12 strikeouts against right-handed pitchers.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> He batted .111 in the 2012 ALCS.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The Yankees were eliminated by the Tigers in the <a href="/wiki/2012_ALCS" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 ALCS">2012 ALCS</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2013">2013</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:5V7A9422_Alex_Rodriguez.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/5V7A9422_Alex_Rodriguez.jpg/220px-5V7A9422_Alex_Rodriguez.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/5V7A9422_Alex_Rodriguez.jpg/330px-5V7A9422_Alex_Rodriguez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/5V7A9422_Alex_Rodriguez.jpg/440px-5V7A9422_Alex_Rodriguez.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1450" data-file-height="1450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:5V7A9422_Alex_Rodriguez.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rodriguez playing for the <a href="/wiki/Trenton_Thunder" title="Trenton Thunder">Trenton Thunder</a>, the Yankees\' AA affiliate, in 2013</div></div></div>\n<p>On January 16, 2013, Rodriguez underwent <a href="/wiki/Arthroscopic_surgery" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthroscopic surgery">arthroscopic surgery</a> in his hip to repair a torn <a href="/wiki/Acetabular_labrum" title="Acetabular labrum">labrum</a>. It was the second time in four years that he had the surgery, although this operation was more serious than before. Rodriguez began the 2013 season on the 60-day <a href="/wiki/Disabled_list" title="Disabled list">disabled list</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While rehabilitating his hip, Rodriguez was embroiled in a series of negative headlines: he became a central figure of the <a href="/wiki/Biogenesis_baseball_scandal" title="Biogenesis baseball scandal">Biogenesis baseball scandal</a> and MLB\'s investigation into his possible connection to performance-enhancing drugs;<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> additionally, after Rodriguez announced on Twitter that his doctor had medically cleared him to play in games, Yankees general manager <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cashman" title="Brian Cashman">Brian Cashman</a> soon revealed that Rodriguez\'s doctor did not have such authority to clear him.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez played his first rehab assignment game on July 2, 2013 with the Yankees Class-A Low affiliate, the <a href="/wiki/Charleston_RiverDogs" title="Charleston RiverDogs">Charleston RiverDogs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> He continued his rehabilitation and played for the Yankees Triple-A team, the <a href="/wiki/Scranton/Wilkes-Barre_RailRiders" title="Scranton/Wilkes-Barre RailRiders">Scranton/Wilkes-Barre RailRiders</a> on July 18.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Two days prior to his scheduled promotion to the major league roster, Rodriguez sustained a new injury, as an MRI later revealed a Grade 1 quad strain, delaying his return and forcing him to continue rehabilitating in the minor leagues. Rodriguez independently sought a second opinion on his quad strain on July 24 with a doctor who stated that there did not appear to be an injury; the Yankees front office was further upset by his decision, claiming that he violated league rules for seeking a second opinion without the team\'s permission.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> He completed his rehabilitation program with the Yankees\' Double-A affiliate <a href="/wiki/Trenton_Thunder" title="Trenton Thunder">Trenton Thunder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez made his 2013 return with the Yankees on August 5, which was the same day that MLB announced he would be suspended\xe2\x80\x94pending an appeal\xe2\x80\x94 through the 2014 season for his role in the Biogenesis scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> On August 11, Rodriguez hit his first home run of the season off <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Justin_Verlander" title="Justin Verlander">Justin Verlander</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> With the home run, Rodriguez passed <a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial" title="Stan Musial">Stan Musial</a> for fifth place in career RBIs.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez continued to feud with Yankees management following his return, as his lawyers accused the team, and specifically <a href="/wiki/Christopher_S._Ahmad" title="Christopher S. Ahmad">Christopher S. Ahmad</a>, of mishandling his hip injury in several ways; Rodriguez\'s legal team contended that the team withheld the injury from him and continued to play him in 2012, despite his health, and that team president <a href="/wiki/Randy_Levine" title="Randy Levine">Randy Levine</a> told Rodriguez\'s hip surgeon that he would feel elated if Rodriguez never played again.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In response to the accusations, Cashman said, "I\'m not comfortable talking to Alex about this because we feel we are in a litigious environment. Hello and goodbye, that\'s about it." He added, "It\'s not just Yankees\' management. He\'s putting it at the level of our trainers, our medical staff. The organization. The team."<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During a game against the Red Sox on August 18, 2013, Rodriguez was involved in key moments against <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Dempster" title="Ryan Dempster">Ryan Dempster</a>. The first time he faced Dempster, Rodriguez was hit by a pitch on a 3-0 count, leading to home plate umpire <a href="/wiki/Brian_O%27Nora" title="Brian O&#39;Nora">Brian O\'Nora</a> warning both benches and ejecting Girardi, while Dempster was allowed to stay in the game. Later in the top of the 6th inning, Rodriguez hit a 442-foot home run to straightway center off Dempster. The Yankees won 9-6, and Dempster, who hit Rodriguez before, was suspended 5 games by the MLB with an undisclosed fine (although he did not miss a start).\n</p><p>On September 20, at <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium" title="Yankee Stadium">Yankee Stadium</a>, Rodriguez hit his 24th career <a href="/wiki/Grand_slam_(baseball)" title="Grand slam (baseball)">grand slam</a>, an opposite field 654th career home run, off <a href="/wiki/George_Kontos" title="George Kontos">George Kontos</a> of the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a>, breaking the all-time grand slam record, formerly held by <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> For the 2013 season, Rodriguez played in only 44 games batting .244 with 7 home runs and 19 RBI.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014">2014</span></h4>\n<p>Rodriguez\'s suspension that was announced the previous season but delayed pending an appeal, was upheld for the entirety of the 2014 regular season and postseason. He was found to have violated the league\'s Performance Enhancing Drugs policy, specifically through the "use and possession of numerous forms of prohibited performance-enhancing substances, including Testosterone and human Growth Hormone, over the course of multiple years" and "attempting to cover-up his violations of the Program by engaging in a course of conduct intended to obstruct and frustrate the Office of the Commissioner\'s investigation."<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>  At the end of the 2014 season, Brian Cashman announced that Rodriguez would no longer serve as an everyday third baseman after the team\'s signing of <a href="/wiki/Chase_Headley" title="Chase Headley">Chase Headley</a>, and would instead become a <a href="/wiki/Designated_hitter" title="Designated hitter">designated hitter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DH_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DH-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2015">2015</span></h4>\n<p>In the off-season, during the week of January 19, 2015, it was reported that Rodriguez met with new <a href="/wiki/Commissioner_of_Baseball" title="Commissioner of Baseball">Commissioner of Baseball</a> <a href="/wiki/Rob_Manfred" title="Rob Manfred">Rob Manfred</a>, resulting in a "positive discussion, lasting 10 minutes in which Rodriguez apologized, while promising to behave in the future".<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>  On February 17, 2015, Rodriguez issued a hand-written letter of apology to "Major League Baseball, the Yankees, the Steinbrenner family, the Players Association and you, the fans".<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez reported to New York Yankees\' 2015 spring training camp three days early.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>  Girardi planned to play Rodriguez at first base during spring training to assess whether he could be played there, a first for his career.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez played his first game after his suspension on opening day against the <a href="/wiki/2015_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="2015 Toronto Blue Jays season">Blue Jays</a> at Yankee Stadium. He served as the designated hitter, going 1 for 2 with a walk as the Yankees lost to the Blue Jays 1\xe2\x80\x936.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>  On April 17, his first multi-HR game \xe2\x80\x93 and third and fourth home runs \xe2\x80\x93 of the season included a blast off <a href="/wiki/Nate_Karns" title="Nate Karns">Nate Karns</a> of <a href="/wiki/2015_Tampa_Bay_Rays_season" title="2015 Tampa Bay Rays season">Tampa Bay</a> that traveled 471 feet (144&#160;m), providing four total RBIs in a 5\xe2\x80\x934 win.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In a pinch-hit appearance against the <a href="/wiki/2015_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2015 Boston Red Sox season">Red Sox</a> on May 1, Rodriguez hit his 660th career home run off reliever <a href="/wiki/Junichi_Tazawa" title="Junichi Tazawa">Junichi Tazawa</a>, tying <a href="/wiki/Willie_Mays" title="Willie Mays">Willie Mays</a> for fourth place on the all-time home run list.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> On May 7, Rodriguez hit his 661st career home run off <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Orioles</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Chris_Tillman" title="Chris Tillman">Chris Tillman</a> for sole possession of fourth place on the all-time home run list.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> On May 27, Rodriguez set an AL record for the most career RBI, passing Lou Gehrig, also moving him into third on the all-time list.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With his 666th career home run against <a href="/wiki/Bud_Norris" title="Bud Norris">Bud Norris</a> of the Orioles on June 13, Rodriguez drove in his 2,000th and 2,001st career runs. However, opinions varied on whether he was the second (<a href="/wiki/Elias_Sports_Bureau" title="Elias Sports Bureau">Elias Sports Bureau</a>, trailing Aaron), third (MLB, trailing Aaron and Ruth),<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> or fourth player (Baseball-Reference.com, trailing Aaron, Ruth, and <a href="/wiki/Cap_Anson" title="Cap Anson">Cap Anson</a>) in MLB history to attain 2,000 RBIs.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez\' next home run was also his <a href="/wiki/3,000_hit_club" title="3,000 hit club">3,000th career hit</a>, making him the 29th player to reach the milestone. He hit it against the <a href="/wiki/2015_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="2015 Detroit Tigers season">Tigers</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Justin_Verlander" title="Justin Verlander">Justin Verlander</a> in a 7\xe2\x80\x932 win, joining <a href="/wiki/Wade_Boggs" title="Wade Boggs">Wade Boggs</a> and Jeter \xe2\x80\x93 both former Yankees \xe2\x80\x93 as the only players to hit a home run for his 3,000th hit.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> With his next hit on June 20, Rodriguez surpassed <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Clemente" title="Roberto Clemente">Roberto Clemente</a>, the eleventh player in MLB history to have recorded 3000 hits.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>  On July 25, against the <a href="/wiki/2015_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="2015 Minnesota Twins season">Twins</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>, and two days before his 40th birthday, Rodr\xc3\xadguez became the fifth-oldest player to hit three home runs in one game.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In his first 95 games of the season, Rodriguez hit 24 homers and produced an OPS of .930.<sup id="cite_ref-mccarron052616_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mccarron052616-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>  After being mired in a 72-at-bat slump without a home run until August 18 against the Twins, he hit his 25th home run which was also his 25th career grand slam, extending his major league record. The home run also drove in the go-ahead runs for an 8\xe2\x80\x934 Yankees win.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_on_August_2,_2016_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Alex_Rodriguez_on_August_2%2C_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Alex_Rodriguez_on_August_2%2C_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="220" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Alex_Rodriguez_on_August_2%2C_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Alex_Rodriguez_on_August_2%2C_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Alex_Rodriguez_on_August_2%2C_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Alex_Rodriguez_on_August_2%2C_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1608" data-file-height="1943" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_on_August_2,_2016_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rodriguez with the Yankees in 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>From August 1 until the end of the season, Rodriguez appeared in 56 games, batting .191, .678 OPS, nine home runs, and struck out 59 times in 183 at-bats.<sup id="cite_ref-mccarron052616_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mccarron052616-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>  The first base experiment yielded two total appearances in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>  He finished with 33 home runs, 86 RBI, 131 hits, and a .252 batting average. He led the Yankees in home runs, on-base percentage, slugging percentage, on-base plus slugging, and bases-on-balls. Rodriguez reached 30+ home runs for the 15th time in his career, tying Aaron for the most 30-home-run seasons in history.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016">2016</span></h4>\n<p>On April 17, 2016, Rodriguez became the 19th player to make 12,000 career <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_career_plate_appearance_leaders" title="List of Major League Baseball career plate appearance leaders">plate appearances</a>. On May 4, the Yankees placed him on the 15-day disabled list due to a right hamstring strain.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>  On May 24, the Yankees sent him on a rehab assignment to the Double-A Trenton Thunder,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> and activated him on May 26.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>  The next day, he hit his 30th career home run at <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Field" title="Tropicana Field">Tropicana Field</a>, which traveled an estimated 440 feet (130&#160;m), as the Yankees defeated <a href="/wiki/2016_Tampa_Bay_Rays_season" title="2016 Tampa Bay Rays season">Tampa Bay</a>, 4\xe2\x80\x931.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>  However, for much of the season, Rodriguez notably struggled to adequately produce, enduring prolonged slumps as his role dwindled from everyday designated hitter to pinch hitter. In July, he had two extra base hits, including his 696th career home run.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cubs_029_(30085597324)_Alex_Rodriguez_Fox_Sports_postgame.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cubs_029_%2830085597324%29_Alex_Rodriguez_Fox_Sports_postgame.jpg/220px-Cubs_029_%2830085597324%29_Alex_Rodriguez_Fox_Sports_postgame.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cubs_029_%2830085597324%29_Alex_Rodriguez_Fox_Sports_postgame.jpg/330px-Cubs_029_%2830085597324%29_Alex_Rodriguez_Fox_Sports_postgame.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cubs_029_%2830085597324%29_Alex_Rodriguez_Fox_Sports_postgame.jpg/440px-Cubs_029_%2830085597324%29_Alex_Rodriguez_Fox_Sports_postgame.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2488" data-file-height="1777" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cubs_029_(30085597324)_Alex_Rodriguez_Fox_Sports_postgame.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rodriquez working as a postgame television commentator during the <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Series" title="2016 World Series">2016 World Series</a></div></div></div>\n<p>At a press conference held on August 7, Rodriguez announced that he would play in his final game for the Yankees on the following Friday, August 12, against the Rays at Yankee Stadium. It was also noted that the Yankees would sign him to a new contract that would keep him in the organization through 2017 as a special instructor and advisor. In the offseason, Rodriguez would join the Yankees\' <a href="/wiki/Front_office" title="Front office">front office</a> as a special advisor.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The club commemorated Rodriguez\'s final game as a Yankee, thanking him in front of a sold-out crowd for his efforts with a tribute of highlights on the stadium videoboard, a presentation of a framed number 13 jersey, and a base autographed by teammates.<sup id="cite_ref-suss081216_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suss081216-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> This was in stark contrast to the year-long farewell tour given to his former Yankee teammate Derek Jeter. At the plate, he batted third and started as the designated hitter, going 1-for-4 with an RBI double. In the ninth inning, he was brought onto the field at third base for one batter \xe2\x88\x92 his only defensive appearance for the Yankees in 2016<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x88\x92 and departed the field to a "raucous ovation" from the fans.<sup id="cite_ref-suss081216_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suss081216-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>  The next day, the Yankees granted him his unconditional release.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rumors swirled regarding Rodriguez\'s future in baseball; the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a> were interested in signing him to play first base until his spokesman Ron Berkowitz emailed the media on August 15 and said on behalf of Rodriguez, "I want to put all this talk to rest about Alex playing for any team this season. It\'s not happening. Like he said Friday night, he is happy and he is going to take some time to relax and hang with his family and friends."<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez ended the season playing 65 games with a .200 batting average, 9 home runs and 31 RBIs.\n</p><p>In January 2017, Rodriguez\'s spokesman said that he would not play for any other team in the coming year, and would remain a "special advisor" to Yankees owner Hal Steinbrenner.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reggie%26A-Rod.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Reggie%26A-Rod.jpg/170px-Reggie%26A-Rod.jpg" width="170" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Reggie%26A-Rod.jpg/255px-Reggie%26A-Rod.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Reggie%26A-Rod.jpg/340px-Reggie%26A-Rod.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1439" data-file-height="1950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reggie%26A-Rod.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> talking with Rodriguez during batting practice</div></div></div>\n<p>Due to the unsuccessful nature of the Yankees postseasons from 2004 to 2007, along with Rodriguez\'s sub-.200 batting average in the postseasons of 2005 and 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-b-r_23-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-r-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez drew criticism in the New York area, both from writers, such as the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">New York Post</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> Joel Sherman, and players, such as then-teammate, Jason Giambi.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sports_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sports-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Prior to 2009, Rodriguez had received the nickname "The Cooler" among some players because of the perceived tendency for teams to turn cold when he joins them and hot when he leaves.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> According to Yankee manager <a href="/wiki/Joe_Torre" title="Joe Torre">Joe Torre</a>\'s 2009 book, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Yankee_Years" title="The Yankee Years">The Yankee Years</a></i>, Rodriguez earned the nickname "A-Fraud" from teammates and particularly from clubhouse attendants who were said to resent his demands.<sup id="cite_ref-Torre_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Torre-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> "It was [said] in front of him", Torre later said of the nickname. "A lot of that stuff that went on in the clubhouse was more tongue-in-cheek, fun type stuff", he explained.<sup id="cite_ref-Torre2_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Torre2-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Much of the criticism regarding Rodriguez focuses on his alleged inability to produce hits in clutch situations.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, Rodriguez hit only .264 with runners in scoring position and two outs. In 95 plate appearances, he walked 20 times and was hit by three pitches, and he had only 19 hits. Of the 41 times Rodriguez struck out with two outs, 20 came with runners in scoring position.<sup id="cite_ref-100random_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100random-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Because of the Yankees\' successful history, he was compared unfavorably to other Yankees greats who have performed exceptionally well in the postseason, such as <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>  However, after his performance in the 2009 postseason, Rodriguez started receiving many positive comparisons to Reggie Jackson, even being selected as "Mr. October" by Jackson and <i>USA Today</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez answered many of the criticisms of his postseason performance by performing exceptionally well in the 2009 postseason, where he posted a .365 batting average and hit six home-runs in 52 at-bats during the Yankees\' 15 post-season games.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_of_performance-enhancing_drugs">Use of performance-enhancing drugs</span></h2>\n<p>In July 2007, former outfielder and <a href="/wiki/Banned_substances_in_baseball" class="mw-redirect" title="Banned substances in baseball">steroid-user</a> <a href="/wiki/Jose_Canseco" title="Jose Canseco">Jose Canseco</a> said that he was planning to publish another book about Major League Baseball, to follow his 2005 bestseller <i><a href="/wiki/Juiced:_Wild_Times,_Rampant_%27Roids,_Smash_Hits_%26_How_Baseball_Got_Big" class="mw-redirect" title="Juiced: Wild Times, Rampant &#39;Roids, Smash Hits &amp; How Baseball Got Big">Juiced: Wild Times, Rampant \'Roids, Smash Hits &amp; How Baseball Got Big</a></i>. Canseco said his new book would have "other stuff" on Rodriguez, and called him a hypocrite.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>  At the time, Rodriguez denied accusations of steroid use.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> In a 2007 interview with <a href="/wiki/Katie_Couric" title="Katie Couric">Katie Couric</a>, Rodriguez flatly denied ever having used performance-enhancing drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-Questions_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Questions-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2009, <a href="/wiki/Selena_Roberts" title="Selena Roberts">Selena Roberts</a> and David Epstein of <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> reported that Rodriguez had tested positive for two <a href="/wiki/Anabolic_steroids" class="mw-redirect" title="Anabolic steroids">anabolic steroids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Testosterone_(medication)" title="Testosterone (medication)">testosterone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Primobolan" class="mw-redirect" title="Primobolan">Primobolan</a>, during his 2003 season playing for the Texas Rangers, the same season in which he captured his first American League <a href="/wiki/Most_Valuable_Player" class="mw-redirect" title="Most Valuable Player">Most Valuable Player</a> award, broke 300 career home runs (hitting 47 that year),<sup id="cite_ref-YankeesPay_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YankeesPay-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> and earned one of his ten <a href="/wiki/Silver_Slugger_Award" title="Silver Slugger Award">Silver Slugger Awards</a>. The information had been part of a government-sealed report detailing 104 <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">major league</a> players (out of 1200 players tested)<sup id="cite_ref-Glanville_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glanville-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> who tested positive for performance enhancers during a 2003 drug <a href="/wiki/Statistical_survey" class="mw-redirect" title="Statistical survey">survey</a>. Approved by the players themselves with the promise of anonymity,<sup id="cite_ref-Glanville_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glanville-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> the survey was conducted by Major League Baseball to see whether a mandatory drug testing program might be necessary. At the time, as the result of a collectively bargained union agreement,<sup id="cite_ref-Glanville_87-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glanville-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> there was no penalty or punishment for a positive test.<sup id="cite_ref-SIsteroids_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SIsteroids-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NBCsteroid_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBCsteroid-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Because more than 5% of the samples taken from players in 2003 came back positive, mandatory testing of major league baseball players began in 2004, with penalties for violations.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTsteroids_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTsteroids-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_2009_World_Series_Parade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Alex_Rodriguez_2009_World_Series_Parade.jpg/220px-Alex_Rodriguez_2009_World_Series_Parade.jpg" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Alex_Rodriguez_2009_World_Series_Parade.jpg/330px-Alex_Rodriguez_2009_World_Series_Parade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Alex_Rodriguez_2009_World_Series_Parade.jpg/440px-Alex_Rodriguez_2009_World_Series_Parade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1139" data-file-height="664" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Rodriguez_2009_World_Series_Parade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alex Rodriguez during the <a href="/wiki/2009_World_Series" title="2009 World Series">2009 World Series</a> parade.</div></div></div>\n<p>The 2003 test results were supposed to remain anonymous and the samples destroyed. However, a coded master list of 104 players was seized during the <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Laboratory_Co-operative" title="Bay Area Laboratory Co-operative">BALCO</a> investigation, turning up in a 2004 federal raid on Comprehensive Drug Testing\'s facility in <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_California" title="Long Beach, California">Long Beach</a>, California. A month later, the physical samples were seized by federal agents raiding <a href="/wiki/Quest_Diagnostics" title="Quest Diagnostics">Quest Diagnostics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas, Nevada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTsteroids_88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTsteroids-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The list of the 104 positive-testing players was released to the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Players_Association" title="Major League Baseball Players Association">Major League Baseball Players Association</a> (MLBPA) in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNadmission_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNadmission-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The players\' union later said that the 104 positive samples were in the process of being destroyed when they were <a href="/wiki/Subpoena" title="Subpoena">subpoenaed</a> by federal authorities in November 2003, making continued destruction "improper."<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_expanation_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_expanation-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although testosterone is available by prescription for some uses, Primobolan has no approved prescription use.<sup id="cite_ref-SIsteroids_86-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SIsteroids-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>  Also known as <i>methenolone</i> or <i>metenolone enanthate</i>, it is the same <a href="/wiki/Steroid" title="Steroid">steroid</a> that <a href="/wiki/Barry_Bonds" title="Barry Bonds">Barry Bonds</a> is alleged to have tested positive for in 2000 and 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTsteroids_88-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTsteroids-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>  A fairly weak steroid on its own, it is generally used in conjunction with other steroids.<sup id="cite_ref-StarLedgersteroids_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StarLedgersteroids-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>  The drug is generally preferred in injected rather than oral form due to its cost.<sup id="cite_ref-StarLedgersteroids_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StarLedgersteroids-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>  An official statement by Major League Baseball made shortly after Rodriguez\'s test results became public expressed "grave concern" without naming Rodriguez, noting that "because the survey testing that took place in 2003 was intended to be non-disciplinary and anonymous, we can not make any comment on the accuracy of this report as it pertains to the player named."<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In an interview with ESPN after the report came out, citing "an enormous amount of pressure to perform", Rodriguez admitted to using banned substances from 2001 to 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNadmission_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNadmission-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> "All my years in New York have been clean", he added, saying he has not used banned substances since last taking them following a spring training injury in 2003 while playing for the Rangers.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNadmission_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNadmission-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTadmission_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTadmission-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>  "Back then, [baseball] was a different culture", Rodriguez said. "It was very loose. I was young, I was stupid, I was na\xc3\xafve. And I wanted to prove to everyone that I was worth being one of the greatest players of all time. I did take a banned substance. And for that, I am very sorry and deeply regretful."<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNadmission_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNadmission-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTadmission_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTadmission-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez said he could not be sure of the name(s) of the substance(s) he had used.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNadmission_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNadmission-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTadmission_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTadmission-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez said he was never told that he was among the 104 players who tested positive, only that a tip came in August 2004 from <a href="/wiki/Gene_Orza" class="mw-redirect" title="Gene Orza">Gene Orza</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Players_Association" title="Major League Baseball Players Association">MLBPA</a> that he "may or may not have" failed his 2003 test.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNadmission_4-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNadmission-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>  Orza is accused by three (unnamed) MLB players of tipping Rodriguez to an upcoming drug test in September 2004. Orza and the MLBPA have denied the allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTdenial_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTdenial-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez absolved the players\' union of any blame for leaking his positive test results, saying he alone was responsible for his mistakes.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNadmission_4-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNadmission-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>  Friend and former teammate <a href="/wiki/Doug_Glanville" title="Doug Glanville">Doug Glanville</a>, while noting the outrage over Rodriguez\'s years of steroid use, berated Rodriguez\'s critics for their "lack of outrage about how a confidential and anonymous test could be made public."<sup id="cite_ref-Glanville_87-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glanville-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>  No Major League player, Glanville wrote, would have participated in the 2003 survey if he had thought the results had even a chance of becoming public. "It has everything to do with privacy. Being A-Rod should not change that fact."<sup id="cite_ref-Glanville_87-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glanville-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>MLB Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Bud_Selig" title="Bud Selig">Bud Selig</a> briefly considered whether or not to punish Rodriguez for his admitted steroid use, citing the illegality of the situation, among other things. However, at the time of the testing there were no punishments for this sort of activity.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, his admission to three years of steroid use could be damaging to his image and legacy.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTadmission_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTadmission-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Later in the month, Rodriguez called a press conference in <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa, Florida</a>, and in the presence of many supportive Yankee teammates, answered reporters\' questions about his 2001\xe2\x80\x932003 steroid use.<sup id="cite_ref-Questions_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Questions-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ARodBlog_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARodBlog-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez said he and a cousin (whom he refused to name) bought an unidentified drug <a href="/wiki/Over-the-counter_drug" title="Over-the-counter drug">over-the-counter</a> in the Dominican Republic, where it is "known on the streets as boli or bollee."<sup id="cite_ref-Questions_174-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Questions-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Transcript_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Transcript-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> At Rodriguez\'s instruction, the cousin transported the drug into the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-JeterDefends_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JeterDefends-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> For six months of the year, Rodriguez injected himself twice monthly with "boli" (a drug name unfamiliar to experts and perhaps a slang term for Primobolan or <a href="/wiki/Dianabol" class="mw-redirect" title="Dianabol">Dianabol</a>, although the latter steroid is taken orally).<sup id="cite_ref-Questions_174-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Questions-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>  Rodriguez said he did not know whether he was using the drug properly or whether it was safe.<sup id="cite_ref-Questions_174-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Questions-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>  Although he "certainly felt more energy", Rodriguez said it would be "hard to say" whether it gave him a competitive edge.<sup id="cite_ref-ARodBlog_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARodBlog-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez said he would become a spokesperson for the <a href="/wiki/Travis_Tygart" title="Travis Tygart">Taylor Hooton foundation</a>, which educates young people about the dangers of steroid use.<sup id="cite_ref-Questions_174-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Questions-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ARodBlog_182-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARodBlog-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>  He has since spoken at schools about the dangers of steroids.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On February 28, 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported that Rodriguez received treatment from Canadian sports doctor <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Galea" title="Anthony Galea">Anthony Galea</a> in March 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-balco_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-balco-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Galea reached a plea agreement for bringing unapproved and mislabled drugs into the United States, including <a href="/wiki/Human_growth_hormone" class="mw-redirect" title="Human growth hormone">human growth hormone</a> (HGH) and <a href="/wiki/Actovegin" title="Actovegin">Actovegin</a>. Galea confirmed to the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> that he treated Rodriguez but said he only prescribed <a href="/wiki/Anti-inflammatories" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-inflammatories">anti-inflammatories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Galea_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Galea-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biogenesis_baseball_scandal">Biogenesis baseball scandal</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Biogenesis_baseball_scandal" title="Biogenesis baseball scandal">Biogenesis baseball scandal</a></div>\n<p>Rodriguez reportedly received HGH from <a href="/wiki/Biogenesis_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Biogenesis of America">Biogenesis of America</a>, an anti-aging clinic in <a href="/wiki/Coral_Gables,_Florida" title="Coral Gables, Florida">Coral Gables, Florida</a> run by Bosch.<sup id="cite_ref-schmidt_04112013_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schmidt_04112013-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>  For much of the summer, it had been expected that Rodriguez would be suspended for his role in the scandal. The first definitive confirmation came on August 3, when MLB rebuffed the players\' union\'s last-minute offer to negotiate. Instead, it gave Rodriguez until the afternoon of August 4 to reach an agreement regarding a suspension or greater punishment for his role in the Biogenesis affair.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On August 5, 2013, MLB suspended Rodriguez from August 8 through the end of the 2014 season for violating the league\'s PED policy. He would originally miss a total of 211 regular-season games plus any postseason games. He was one of 13 players suspended for their roles in the scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> In its official statement, MLB said that the suspension was based on Rodriguez\'s "use and possession of numerous forms of prohibited performance-enhancing substances, including Testosterone and human Growth Hormone, over the course of multiple years" and "for attempting to cover-up his violations of the Program by engaging in a course of conduct intended to obstruct and frustrate the Office of the Commissioner\'s investigation."<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Although the standard punishment for a first offense under MLB\'s drug policy is 50 games, MLB had the option of suspending Rodriguez for longer than that under the collective bargaining agreement if it determined his actions constituted conduct detrimental to baseball.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Almost immediately after the suspension was announced, Rodriguez announced that he would appeal. He was the only player to do so; the others accepted season-ending 50-game suspensions without appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Although MLB Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Bud_Selig" title="Bud Selig">Bud Selig</a> had the option of using his best-interests-of-baseball powers to remove Rodriguez from the field immediately, he chose to suspend Rodriguez under the drug agreement and not the CBA, allowing Rodriguez to continue playing while the appeal was underway. The proposed suspension would include a global lock clause, which would also prevent him from  playing in other known leagues, such as <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Professional_Baseball" title="Nippon Professional Baseball">Nippon Professional Baseball</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Korea_Baseball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Korea Baseball Championship">Korea Baseball Championship</a> for example, as the leagues in those nations honor any suspensions imposed by MLB.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez hired New York criminal defense lawyer Joe Tacopina.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A lengthy arbitration process followed, but the suspension was upheld on January 11, 2014. However, since Rodriguez was allowed to play during the appeal process, this effectively reduced the suspension to 162 games \xe2\x80\x93 the entirety of the 2014 regular-season schedule. Because Rodriguez was on the suspended list retroactive through August 31, the suspension would have included the postseason if the Yankees qualified (but did not qualify that year). He subsequently issued a statement saying he would be challenging the decision in federal court.<sup id="cite_ref-162games_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162games-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> On February 7, 2014 Rodriguez announced that he was dropping his lawsuit and accepting his suspension for the 2014 season.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> In March 2014, multiple sources reported that Rodriguez was refusing to pay the balance of his legal fees for his defense, which amounted to over $3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> In July 2014, Rodriguez was in fact sued by his lawyers for $380,000 in unpaid legal fees.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2014, it was revealed that back in January Rodriguez had admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration" title="Drug Enforcement Administration">Drug Enforcement Administration</a> that he had used performance-enhancing drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> This was contrary to his sentiments of 18 days earlier, when he had vehemently denied the allegations and also denied having used human growth hormones.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>\n<p>Rodriguez grew up with two half-siblings, Joe and Suzy, who were born in the Dominican Republic and are children from his mother\'s first marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-curry_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curry-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez also has a half-brother, Victor M. Rodriguez, who was born to Alex\'s father Victor Sr. and his then-wife Pouppe Martinez in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-curry_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curry-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> The couple divorced a year later, and Victor Jr. was raised by his mother.<sup id="cite_ref-curry_201-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curry-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> Victor Jr., who is an officer in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a>, fell out of touch with Alex for a period of 23 years, until they met at a <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a> game in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-curry_201-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curry-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> His nephew, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Dunand" class="mw-redirect" title="Joe Dunand">Joe Dunand</a>, is a professional baseball player.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-date-and-last-name_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-date-and-last-name-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> he married Cynthia Scurtis,<sup id="cite_ref-date-and-last-name_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-date-and-last-name-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a> graduate<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> he had met at a gym in <a href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami, Florida">Miami, Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The couple\'s first child, Natasha Alexander, was born on November 18, 2004. On April 21, 2008, Cynthia gave birth to their second child, Ella Alexander,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> in Miami, Florida.\n</p><p>Cynthia Rodriguez filed for divorce on July 7, 2008, citing "<a href="/wiki/Abandonment_(emotional)" title="Abandonment (emotional)">emotional abandonment</a>" of her and their children, as well as "extra marital&#32;&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>&#93; affairs and other marital misconduct" by her husband.<sup id="cite_ref-thesmokinggun.com_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesmokinggun.com-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez responded in court documents that the marriage was "irretrievably broken" but requested that allegations of his "extramarital affairs" be stricken from court records.<sup id="cite_ref-divorce_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divorce-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> The couple reached a settlement that September.<sup id="cite_ref-divorce_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divorce-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> In July, <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> responded to rumors of an affair with Rodriguez by issuing a statement saying, "I am not romantically involved in any way with Alex Rodriguez" and has "nothing to do with the state of his marriage".<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of February 2017, he has been dating <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez used to own a <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> dealership in <a href="/wiki/League_City,_Texas" title="League City, Texas">League City, Texas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> and in his free time, Rodriguez buys and collects art.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> He is an investor for <a href="/wiki/ESports" class="mw-redirect" title="ESports">eSports</a> team <a href="/wiki/NRG_Esports" title="NRG Esports">NRG Esports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As previously mentioned, Rodriguez and Jeter\'s friendship had cooled in recent years. However as of  2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alex_Rodriguez&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, they have grown close again.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alex_Rodriguez&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Rodriguez is represented by sports agent <a href="/wiki/Dan_Lozano" title="Dan Lozano">Dan Lozano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SI_ARod_Agent_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SI_ARod_Agent-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity">Charity</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A-Rod2_adjusted.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/A-Rod2_adjusted.jpg/170px-A-Rod2_adjusted.jpg" width="170" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/A-Rod2_adjusted.jpg/255px-A-Rod2_adjusted.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/A-Rod2_adjusted.jpg/340px-A-Rod2_adjusted.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1476" data-file-height="2337" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A-Rod2_adjusted.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rodriguez takes batting practice in 2009</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2003, Rodriguez gave $3.9&#160;million to the University of Miami to renovate its baseball stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_Rodriguez_Miami_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN_Rodriguez_Miami-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> The new facility was renamed "<a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez_Park_at_Mark_Light_Field" title="Alex Rodriguez Park at Mark Light Field">Alex Rodriguez Park at Mark Light Field</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_Rodriguez_Miami_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN_Rodriguez_Miami-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez remains an ardent University of Miami fan.<sup id="cite_ref-NYPost_Miami_Fan_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYPost_Miami_Fan-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> Despite not having attended the school, he received the University of Miami\'s <a href="/wiki/Edward_T._Foote_II" title="Edward T. Foote II">Edward T. Foote II</a> Alumnus of Distinction Award in 2007 as an honorary alumnus.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> Rodriguez had previously been named an "honorary alumnus" of the university in 2004. He is a member of the University of Miami\'s Board of Trustees.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span></h3>\n<p>Rodriguez was featured in a <a href="/wiki/Pepsi_Cola" class="mw-redirect" title="Pepsi Cola">Pepsi Cola</a> commercial as a truck driver in a fleet of delivery trucks simulating players in a baseball game. At the end of the commercial when he drives his vehicle to make a catch, he is told by his approving partner in the truck that he has a future in the beverage delivery business.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodriguez is featured in a commercial for <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_World_Tour" title="Guitar Hero World Tour">Guitar Hero World Tour</a></i>, where he plays the guitar along with athletes <a href="/wiki/Tony_Hawk" title="Tony Hawk">Tony Hawk</a> on drums, <a href="/wiki/Kobe_Bryant" title="Kobe Bryant">Kobe Bryant</a> on vocals, and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Phelps" title="Michael Phelps">Michael Phelps</a> on guitar. The commercial is a spoof of the scene from <i><a href="/wiki/Risky_Business" title="Risky Business">Risky Business</a></i> where <a href="/wiki/Tom_Cruise" title="Tom Cruise">Tom Cruise</a> is dancing to "<a href="/wiki/Old_Time_Rock_and_Roll" title="Old Time Rock and Roll">Old Time Rock and Roll</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><b>Championships earned or
